Welcome, Adventurer!

You are reading the web version of a choose your own adventure book, you lucky thing.

My wife and I often read gamebooks in the Fighting Fantasy series together, and those pioneering stories were one of my first tastes of the weird and wonderful world of RPGs.

This gamebook specifically is heavily inspired by the fantastic boardgame The Mystic Wood, created by Terence Peter Donnelly. It's a game of exploration, steeped in Arthurian legend, where you play as 1 of 7 heroes each with their own quest to complete. My partner loves this game, so if you encounter a reference you don't quite get, it's probably either a Mystic Wood allusion or an in-joke between us.

One day, I will work in proper RPG functionality to this web version. For now, I encourage you to use a physical pen, paper, and dice. Track your stats and inventory, draw a map, go nuts. But, if you're anything like me, you'll read this like a book 9 times out of 10 and ignore the RPG elements. Don't worry, I won't tell on you.

To skip the rules explanation and jump to the story, click here: Background

Click any bold and underlined text to take you to that reference.

To go back to the previous reference, use the back function in your browser.

For a handy reference to loot tables, equipment descriptions, and more, click the sword and staff icon in the top left of your screen.




For Claire




CHARACTER CREATION

Before embarking on your adventure, you must first create your character by deciding your Stats, Class, and starting Feats. These three elements will be explained below and then you will find instructions on how to create your hero after.

Stats

Heroes are defined by three key characteristics:

PROWESS - This reflects your skill in combat, whether that be the deftness of your blade arm or the potency of your magic. This stat directly impacts how often you will strike your foes, and the damage you will deal upon them.

CONSTITUTION - Your hardiness, stamina, and fortitude. This stat defines your total maximum health.

CHARISMA - Your skills at persuasion and creating trust from thin air. The denizens of the Mystic Wood are less likely to attack strangers they like, and they're more likely to provide clues or equipment as well.

Class

Heroes come in two forms: WARRIORS , and WIZARDS .

WARRIORS are experts in martial combat. They are fast, precise, and wield weaponry like extensions of their own arms. Their Feats largely focus around dealing and sustaining greater amounts of damage.

WIZARDS are beings who are tapped into the magic underlying all life. They have the rare gift of manipulating those arcane threads to create elements from thin air, or to discombobulate foes. Their Feats generally focus around using magical energy to gain unconventional advantages in combat.

Feats

A FEAT is a heroic ability that has been awakened inside you. These can take the form of magical spells, a deep knowledge of a subject, or an act of physical strength or dexterity that few can perform.

Each class has a set of Feats that they can learn, but only start with knowledge of very few. Heroes can earn more feats throughout this adventure, if they can awaken the power inside them that is...

Assigning stats

To create your character, you must first decide your starting skill levels. You have 30 POINTS to distribute between your PROWESS, CONSTITUTION, and CHARISMA stats. You could create a balanced hero by equally distributing these points between the three, or specialise your hero in one or the other. Either route is entirely viable.

You may also define these initial stats by rolling a D20 for each one, but be wary of entering the forest as a hero too weak or indeed too powerful.

For your Constitution, double the value you assign to it and mark that down as your hero's starting maximum health. When recovering your health throughout the adventure, you may never exceed this number except in the rare cases where the text specifies you may.

Choosing a class

You must next choose the class of hero you would like to play as. Broadly, WARRIORS will excel in fighting enemies and WIZARDS will have access to a variety of skills that will benefit them outside of combat more so than in combat.

If you have chosen a Warrior, you may start your adventure with an Axe (+1 Prowess), Sword (+1 Constitution), or Pair of Daggers (+1 Charisma). You may find other weapons or armour in your travels but remember that you only gain the benefits of the one you are wielding.

If you have chosen a Wizard, you must have a Focus in order to use most magic. A Focus is much like a wand and allows you to direct magical energy. You may start with an Oak Focus (+1 Prowess), a Redwood Focus (+1 Constitution), or a Walnut Focus (+1 Charisma). As above, you may find other Focusi or armour on your travels, but you only gain the benefits of what you are using. By default, your Focus deals damage through ranged blasts of energy.

Feats

Warriors and Wizards have a different pool of feats to choose from. Based on the class you chose, refer to the relevant table below and pick TWO abilities to enter this adventure with. You may choose these randomly by rolling a D20 twice, or you may choose more or fewer Feats if you would like to mix up future adventures into these woods.

Skill checks

Throughout your adventure, you will be asked to roll against one of your stats to determine if you succeed or fail certain tasks. To do this, roll a D20 and if the result is equal to or less than the stat being tested, then you succeed. If you roll a number greater than the value of your stat, you have failed that test.

Warrior feats

1. Harden Skin - Once per combat, halve incoming damage. May be used in reaction to an attack.

2. Throw Rock - Once per combat, roll a D20 and divide the result by 4, rounding down. Deal that damage to your opponent for free.

3. Surgical Precision - Once per combat, before you roll for your Attack Strength, you may choose to add +3 to the next roll.

4. Battlefield Repairs - Once per combat, recover 1 Health. Also gives you the ability to repair items you may encounter in the world.

5. Musical Ability - Grants you knowledge of musical theory and musical instruments.

6. Bulwark - Once per combat, reduce incoming damage by half of your Constitution.

7. Feint - Once per combat, after losing an attacking roll, you may add +4 to your attack if it will allow you to win that round of combat.

8. Keen Sight - Gives you the ability to notice things that others may miss. Once per combat, allows you to predict an enemy's movements and deduct 2 from their attacking dice roll.

9. Amphibian Seduction - Makes you strangely appealing to Amphibians.

10. Guile - Once per combat, and before you roll for Attack Strength, you may add half of your Charisma stat to your next roll.

11. Disarming Smile - Once per combat, after you lose an attack round, you may deduct half your Charisma stat from the incoming damage.

12. Caltrops - Once per combat, throw Caltrops onto the ground which cause 1 damage to your foe every turn, regardless of the results of Attack Strength rolls.

13. Dense Muscle - Add 1 to your Prowess.

14. Born Digger - You are naturally adept at digging holes quickly and without causing damage to yourself.

15. Favourite Customer - Once per merchant, reduce the cost of a single item by half of your Charisma stat.

16. Intimidate - Once per combat, and before rolling for an opponent’s Attack Strength, you may halve your opponent's next Attack Strength roll.

17. Hilt bash - Once per combat, you may add your Constitution divided by 4 to an Attack Strength roll.

18. Eye for Glitter - Whenever you gain gold, you find 1 more Gold Piece than is stated.

19. Rationer - Whenever you find items of food, you find 1 more item of food than is stated.

20. Sixth Sense - You can inherently detect dark magical auras.

Wizard feats

1. Magic Missile - Once per combat, you may roll a D20, divide the result by 4 (rounding down), and send out that many magical bolts that deal 1 damage each to a foe of your choice.

2. Create Slime - You can generate slime from the ground. Once per combat, and before an enemy rolls for their Attack Strength, you may reduce their next Attack Strength roll by 3.

3. Lightning Bolt - Once per combat, and before rolling for your Attack Strength, you may add +2 to your next Attack Strength roll.

4. Create Gale - You can create great gusts of wind. Once per combat, instead of attacking, you may summon a gale. Your opponent must roll against their Prowess. If they succeed, they attack as normal. If they fail, they are unable to attack for 1 round.

5. Strange Frog Attraction - Your latent magical energies make you oddly attractive to frogs.

6. Create Water - You can create water from nothing.

7. Reform and Repair - Once per combat, recover 1 health. Also allows you to repair items and objects in the world.

8. Move Earth - Allows you magically shift dirt rather than dig it away manually.

9. Charm Person - After failing a Charisma roll, you may add a number divisible by 2 to the number you rolled in order to succeed. This emergency magic will cost you half the value added in health, however.

10. Enhance Eyes - Temporarily enhance your vision to notice things that others may miss. Once per combat, allows you to predict an enemy's movements and deduct 2 from their Attack Strength dice roll.

11. Generate Intense Heat - Allows you to superheat an item or yourself. Once per combat, use this spell to deal 2 damage in retaliation if you receive damage.

12. Ear For Music - You have a natural affinity for musical theory and musical instruments.

13. Thin Skin - Once per combat, you may roll against your Charisma. If you succeed, you curse your foe with thin skin, causing them to take 3 extra damage from each attack for 3 rounds.

14. Stone Skin - Once per combat, halve incoming damage. May be used in reaction to an attack.

15. Alchemy - Whenever you gain gold, you find 1 more Gold Piece than is stated.

16. Battlefield Brigand - Once per combat, you may roll against your Charisma instead of attacking. If you succeed, your opponent gives you 1D20 divided by four (rounded down) worth of Gold. If you fail, they attack as normal.

17. Magically Enhanced Bribery - Once per merchant, you may use any number of food or gold to reduce the cost of an item by that amount.

18. Big Wizard - Once per combat, you may magically double in size. This allows you to deal 1.5 times more damage per successful attack, but you also receive 1.5 times more damage from successful enemy attacks.

19. Detect Evil - You can inherently detect dark magical auras.

20. Sipper - You get 1 extra use out of every potion you drink, to be used whenever you wish.

Advice on Adventuring

Fighting Denizens

When you enter into combat, you must resolve the fight as described below. First, note your opponent's Prowess and Health in your adventuring notes to track how they may change throughout the battle.

0. Note any feats that you may want to use in this battle, and when you are able to use them.

1. Roll a D20 for your opponent and add its Prowess to that number. This is your foe's Attack Strength.

2. Roll a D20 for yourself and add your Prowess to that number. This is your Attack Strength.

3. The combatant with the higher number gets a strike in, and the difference between the two numbers is the amount of damage dealt. If both numbers are the same, then you have parried each other’s attacks and no damage is dealt. Combat continues from step 1 above.

4. Subtract the damage dealt from the health stat of the combatant that lost the round of combat.

5. Begin the next Attack Round, starting again at step 1. This flow repeats until either you or your opponent reach 0 health (death).

If you are killed, you may either retry the battle from its initial values or deny yourself mercy and start your adventure again using a new character.

Provisions and Recovering Health

There are two types of Provision that you will find on your adventure: items of Food, and Full Rations.

An item of Food on its own is not enough to provide a filling meal, but 6 food items is more substantial. A bundle of 6 food items is considered a Ration, but it is recommended that you track food you find in Food Items rather than Rations.

At any time that you feel safe to do so, you may eat a portion of Rations and recover 4 health. You may eat as many portions as you like per rest but must deduct 6 Food Items from your total for each Ration that you eat.

Loot

Throughout your adventure you will have the opportunity to explore the hiding places of the forest, and perhaps the pockets of those you fell. At times, you will be told that you find some number of COMMON, UNCOMMON, or RARE loot. In order to discover exactly what you find, turn to the back of the book and roll against the loot tables there. For each table, roll a D20 and divide the result by 2, rounding down, then add the corresponding item to your inventory.

For weapons and potions obtained from the loot tables, you can only obtain them once. If you roll that item again, you may re-roll until you find something else.

Equipment

As an adventurer, your equipment is your lifeline. The right weapon or headgear could save your life in the direst of circumstances, but remember this: you can only have one weapon or piece of armour equipped at a time, and you may not switch equipment during a battle. Try to anticipate the challenges ahead of you and change equipment in the calm before the storm.

Background

You are one of the last existing Bunnyborn: creatures descended from the Palapin, a race of hyper-intelligent rabbits that hopped and thrived in the wilderness long ago. When humans entered their lands, tension followed. One species sought to maintain nature and the other to bend it to their will, and yet a pact of peace was formed on the foundation of mutual respect. The humans envied the Palapin's magical prowess, and the Palapin admired the human sense of adventure and courage. Through potent Palapin magic, the Bunnyborn were created as a combination of each species' best traits.

The Palapin disappeared from the world long ago, with no clear reason as to why. No known threat scared them away, no known war wiped them out. The only clue as to what happened is the tale of one farmer boy, who described a great migration of bunnies skyward, towards the brightest moon he had ever seen.

The Bunnyborn remained but were few in number. Without the Palapin, their wilderness home felt cold and empty and so they became a nomadic species. They travelled the land in search of their Palapin ancestors, seeking out adventure wherever it may be found.

It is a rite of passage in Bunnyborn societies to leave the herd when you come of age, only to return when you have a great adventure to tell - for the one thing Bunnyborn enjoy more than adventure is tales of it.

You came of age some months ago and have been journeying since. Your natural agility has served you well on your hikes, traversing over mountains and plains with an incredible diversity of terrain in between. But, despite your keen hearing and eyesight, there has been no adventure to behold, and any human settlement you find greets you with uncertainty from adults and excitable cuddling from the younglings.

But that changed in the small town of Middleturf. You were stretched out on your back, basking in the warm sun, when a woman approached . She was middle-aged, with a hood wrapped tight around her head and a look of abject sadness on her face.

"Yer an adventurer," she said. "All you fluffy tails are, and if that be the case then I need yer help." There was an urgency to her voice that drew you in.

"Y'see, it's my boy... my boy has been lost for an age and I need to know what happened. He went into the forest, the enchanted one, down yonder," she appealed while gesturing towards the Northlands. "Was there to pick mushrooms he was but never returned, and the very night he left there was these great plumes of the vilest, blackest smoke that erupted up from deep in them woods."

"Find him, I beg of ye. And if goodwill is not enough for ye to help, know this: that forest is said to hold great treasures within. Great magics. Great threats as well, I give ye that, but you seem like you can handle yourself plenty."

You considered the strange woman's words carefully, but to any of your kind the promise of adventure is too great a pull to resist. You thanked the woman kindly for the guidance and offered to investigate her son's location. Your words sent her near to tears and she practically pushed six Food Items and 25 Gold Pieces into your hands.

Adventure, it seems, had found you. Without sparing another moment, you followed the woman's directions towards that mysterious forest with a song in your heart.

Continue to 1 .

1

Following the strange woman's directions takes you near on half a day, orange wisps of sunset soon teasing the sky as you march. You press on regardless, knowing that you can simply camp on the forest's edge if night should fall and then pick up your adventure in the morning.

Sunset is in full swing as you reach the apex of a hill and finally see a thick line of ancient trees less than a mile away. So dense is the old growth that you simply can't see anything beyond a few feet into the tree line, but your excitement at reaching your goal overcomes you.

At full sprint you descend the hill, your legs propelling you at great speed while your sharp eyes focus only on where your next footfall will land.

In your haste, you don't even notice that time seems to reverse the closer you get to those woods. When you finally slow to a stop before the trees, it feels like you're in that warm full sun that you were enjoying just hours ago. This forest is not only enchanted, but those enchantments seem to bend reality itself. A fine adventure must surely be ahead!

You look back towards the hill that you just descended, pondering the sudden change in time for just a moment and, when you look to the forest again, the trees themselves seem to have moved.

No longer is there a solid, thick treeline inviting you to clamber over roots and forge new paths, but a clear entryway is now right there in front of you. It's as wide as you are tall, and there is no way that you could have missed it moments ago.

Despite it being full sun, you could camp and see if anything changes by turning to 153 . You may also mistrust that surprise entrance and seek another path into the forest by turning to 588 . Or you might sprint towards adventure and enter the forest at 26 .

2

"Such a wise choice," Madame Duponte grins, clasping her hands together to collect the full nine Gold Pieces you give her. "The code is 7, 4, and 9. Truly, it has been a pleasure relieving you of greed's temptation."

"You have the full code, dear traveller. I bid you safe passage, in this time and the next. But oh, do be careful. I have heard such awful noises from down in that cellar."

"Or perhaps there is information of mine you would like, in exchange for gold of course?"

"How do I cross the river?"

"Where is the missing boy?"

"What is the beast of black smoke?"

Turn to 518

Turn to 382

Turn to 533

Of course, stepping away from the thieving stranger is also an option (turn to 425 ).

3

You sit and ponder whether you should be making a move for some time. The chair gets increasingly hot, and you can feel sores developing on your legs, but the debate continues in your mind. Lose 3 health.

After all, this chair is the safest you've felt since you entered these woods. There are no monsters here, there is no risk. You have everything you need, so why would you move?

Because your adventure demands it, you suppose... Roll against your Prowess + 3. If you succeed, turn to 480 . If you fail, turn to 613 .

4

Marfisa storms out of her tent, blade in hand and the utmost fury upon her face. She sees you free from your bindings and scowls. "So, it comes to this, then," she spits.

There is no way out of this clearing except through her. Prepare yourself.

If you wish to find your own weapon, Marfisa will most certainly get a free hit in on you as you do (roll 1D20 / 2).

MARFISA

Prowess 11

Health 10

Marfisa is easily discouraged. For every two rounds of combat you win in a row, her Prowess is reduced by 2.

If you succeed, turn to 541 .

5

It feels like you span half the forest in following the wolf, but you never leave this area of melted trees and destruction. You assume, then, that you've just been heading on a complicated and circling route. Else the forest is more destroyed than you thought, and that is not a prospect to dwell on.

The wolf pauses above a ledge and carefully climbs down out of your view. You walk around to follow it and see that what was once a natural ridge made of stone and soil now looks unnaturally like paint - with droplets frozen in time dripping over the lip. An ocean's wave but made of earth and forest.

And in the cover beneath the arc of that wave... is a nest. The disfigured wolf is there, tending to three small pups. Each one is grey and unharmed with vibrant blue eyes. Likely born after the catastrophe that this section of forest succumbed to.

On giving your offered food to the pups - who lunge on it hungrily - the adult turns its attention to you. With its snout it nudges a bundle of fabric towards you, and you open it with measured movements. Inside are two lots of Uncommon Loot.

The adult wolf settles down with its family to rest and you suddenly feel like you're intruding. Time to make your way back to the main path.

Turn to 617 .

6

The thatched roof of the hut is tall and overhangs the wooden walls beneath by some margin, making it look like some kind of great wizard's hat. The door is made of several wide planks and is about a head shorter than you are. But, up close like this, you can make out the sound of somewhat raspy music.

You could sneak around and peer into a window (turn to 421 )? Or knock on the door and see who answers (turn to 525 )?

Or you could step away from the hut and travel to the South ( 370 ), the East ( 573 ), or the North ( 595 ).

7

You climb the edge of the crater, though the raised soil is so brittle that you may as well have walked through the rim instead of over it. The bowl is then a challenge to scramble down and you spend as much time sliding down with a cloud of dust behind you as you do carefully planting your feet.

At the centre of the still smoking crater is what looks like a rabbit. As large as you and curled up into a ball as if safely in a nest. But… There are no rabbits this large, not anymore.

The rabbit's ears perk up suddenly, rotating towards you as if it could detect your racing thoughts. Your heart beats ceaselessly against the inside of your ribs as the rabbit lifts its head and meets your eyes. You can't believe it, but... this is a Palapin. The ancient race that gave rise to yours, but they deserted this world long ago...

"Hello, child," you hear inside your own mind. A melodic voice, and calming. The gentle tones of a mother to her child. "I am glad I found you."

As the rabbit rises, stretches, and sits before you, you try your best to find appropriate words.

Turn to 261 .

8

The crone doesn't even hear you approach over her noisome mining efforts and you dispatch her with a single blow. Whatever she was doing was of an unsavoury nature and you're sure she wouldn't have reacted well to being caught.

On her body, you find a strange little stone device. It's triangular in shape, made up of many layers that can each independently rotate. You don't know what to make of it, so you stow it away.

You'll never know what the crone was doing down here, but you suppose there's nothing stopping you using your last swig of that foul drink at least.

Turn to 536 .

9

A knot of magical energy wells inside you, travelling from the core of your being down your arm, and through the conduit you hold. It erupts at the ring in a great blast that ripples the leaves in the trees above... But does not move the ring or note.

"The hells you done that for?" the woman snaps, scowling at you. "I tell you it absorbs magic and you just have to see for yourself. You sneezed and my head'd be gone, you think of that?"

You could say: "It could still be unenchanted though," ( 313 ).

Or you could examine the ring in more detail (turn to 600 ).

10

You dig your feet into the dirt and heave the boat towards the water. It was more entrenched than you realised and your legs are burning with the effort by the time you finish, but you do finish. The boat starts bobbing on the shallow water of the shore and you carefully check for any leaks on your patchwork repairs. They seem to be holding tight, so you push the boat out a little farther and throw yourself in.

If you have the means to create a gust of wind, you could do so now to speed up your journey (turn to 69 ). Otherwise, you'll need to row your way across (turn to 98 ).

11

You march on for some time, but the forest here feels different somehow. The paths are less distinct than before, less certain. You travel down one road, the pattern of trees repeating over and over as if the same tract of land were being taken from behind you and placed in front. You try stacking stones here and there so you know if you truly do loop on yourself, but you never encounter those markers again. At other times the path branches in four, five, sometimes eight directions with each one looking the same as the next. You can't hear a difference between them, you can't smell or sense anything to help orient you, so you take paths at random, only to end up at the same junction you just left more often than not.

The magic in the woods here is confused, and you fear you'll be wandering until you simply can't anymore...

Press on, as long as it takes (turn to 415 ), stop and stay where you are (turn to 190 ), or shout for help (turn to 553 ).

12

Perceval grows suddenly still, and a wild look fogs his eyes. "You have it? The grail?!" He speaks with sudden urgency.

He rushes to you and grabs your hand with his, meeting your eyes. "Well, you are a truly lucky sort, truly. You must tell me about the adventure. Tell me everything."

You spy the boy reaching to his hip with his other hand, fingers searching for the hilt of his dagger. On instinct you push him back and he falls to the floor. Suddenly enraged, he stands and withdraws a full slender blade from his belt.

"You are not leaving here with that grail. It's mine. Mine alone. Feel my wrath, beast!"

PERCEVAL

Prowess 4

Health 10

Perceval is a sneaky combatant. If you succeed a combat roll by 2 or less, Perceval counterattacks you for the same damage.

If you survive the encounter, turn to 521 .

13

Roland is a giant man and he strikes the ground as you'd expect: with an immense and resounding thump. You waste no time in searching his pockets, finding 4 Gold Pieces, two Common Loot, and one Uncommon Loot.

You also remove that amulet from around his neck and run your fingers over the dragon head emblazoned on its face. The medallion is heavier than you'd expect, perhaps weighed down by the immense magical potential you sense within it. You can access a mere fraction of the power, and that already invigorates you (roll to gain 1 Trait).

You could also take Roland's Sword, or Roland's Helmet, both of which can be found in the Special Items section.

With that done, all you can do now is travel along the wide main road either North (turn to 39 ), or South (turn to 342 ). Or walk down one of the narrower cobblestone paths to the East (turn to 557 ), or the West (turn to 398 ).

14

"One right, one wrong," the stranger says. "It all comes down to this last roll. A simple game, not without excitement, eh?"

"Let's see if you're feeling lucky friend," Rogue says and rolls once more with a flourish. The symbol for the number fifteen points skyward.

Choose whether you think the next number will be higher or lower than fifteen, then roll your dice. If the result is equal to fifteen, roll until it isn't.

If you bet correctly, turn to 539 . If you bet incorrectly, turn to 450 .

15

It's exactly as you had heard: the roots seem to wind and converge in a very specific way here, creating what seems to be a tunnel running underground towards the river. This might just be your way across, though you're far too large to fit in that tunnel currently...

If you have mushrooms in your bag, turn to 86 .

Otherwise, you'll have to turn back for now (turn to 136 ).

16

Despite this halflings air of rather impressive danger, you see a vulnerability inside. An insecure man, grappling with pain and uncertainty and unleashing all that internal chaos on the world. You certainly can't be intimidated by him, for you see his threats to be little more than a mask.

"It's okay, Phil," you say. The halfling uncrosses his arms and blinks at you.

"What are you talking about, get out of here before I see how many times I can fold you," he replies.

"You must be so tired, always pushing yourself like this. You’ve worked so hard; you deserve a rest."

Phil seems baffled, taken off guard. He clenches and then unclenches a fist.

"You're a good person, Phil," you say. "I fear that the world has been unkind to you, but you are so much stronger than them. Though even the strongest should take time to relax now and then."

The balding man scrunches his face and clenches both fists this time. He starts advancing towards you at shocking speed for a man his size...

Turn to 393 .

17

You walk away from the large flat stones of the bridge and the terrifying man guarding it with some haste. Stepping back onto the cobblestone path is something of a relief as it means you've put some distance between yourself and Phil.

Turn to 483 .

18

Flickering oranges and a burning heat fills your mind, and you channel that psychic energy outward. You will it into the fallen beams, you stoke it with your mind, and soon the glowing flickers of embers dance across the wood. They grow brighter, and brighter, and then the detritus bursts into flames!

For a moment, you're elated... But then you see the fire crawl up over the wooden beam and dance across the ceiling. The flames travel downwards too, creeping along the floor.

Almost as soon as you realise what you've done, the thick smoke fills your lungs and you've no time to consider or regret it. You're to burn alive in this inn.

Your adventure ends here.

19

The man sighs deeply and hangs his head. "Yeah yeah, fine. Right then..."

He steps forward and withdraws a dagger from his hip. He passes it to you and holds his hand out, giving you the right angle to run a clean slice across his palm. His blood drips into the device and, quickly, he takes the dagger back to do the same to you (lose 2 Health). Your blood is darker than his, but the machine absorbs both just as greedily.

Turn to 504 .

20

As you walk, you spy thin mushrooms worming their way up between cobblestones, and increasingly common and thick tendrils of a strange off-white colour. By the time the cobblestone path gives way to dirt, you are walking a route made almost entirely of those creeping tentacles.

Turn to 317 .

21

The nobles fall to the ground hard, a puff of wig dust bursting into the air from each impact then drifting away on the wind. With the nobles defeated, you may as well see what they were carrying.

Roll once against the Common Loot table, and once against the Uncommon Loot table. You also find 4 Gold Pieces in one of their shoes.

Unfortunately, their wands seem to lose all magical power when you pick them up. Perhaps they were linked to the nobles somehow, or maybe they were simply conduits for a magical power that existed inside them already. You accept that you may never know and throw the wands aside.

You can now travel North at 133 , or East at 173 .

22

Travelling down the stairs is much easier than travelling up them, but you're still breathless when you reach the fine wooden floors of the living quarters.

Examine the bookcase ( 238 ). Examine the seating area ( 362 ). Examine the kitchen ( 477 ). Examine the ornate mirror ( 615 ).

Climb the winding staircase ( 367 ).

Leave the tower and travel East ( 342 ), or West ( 77 ).

23

You fill a cup and a tendril of slime whips out to grab it, tossing the drink and the vessel into its open, gooey maw. It doesn't take long for the creature to start quivering and sinking down. It quivers more, and more, and then starts fading from its deep green colour to an unnatural dark blue. "Ah-ler-gic" it manages to burble before becoming still.

"Tough luck, rabbit," the bartender calls from down the bar. "You had a heck of a run, but you're not quite at my level. Shifts over for you, go get some rest."

With that, he escorts you back over the bar, amongst the throngs of patrons. You'll have to find another way to get the rest of the cellar door code...

Turn to 425 .

24

In a wide clearing, the edge of which is marked by melted trees and ones cracked and destroyed by blunt force, is a ginormous skeleton. It simply seems to be a mess of bones at first, long and short, reaching this way and that. But then you discern the remains of two great wings, stretching to the treeline either side. That helps you identify the creature's body, its great claws, its fearsome skull... These are the remains of a dragon.

Curiously, the bones are obscured and gripped by vines all over. They burst from the dirt in thick arms and grasp at the dead animal, coiling many times around its limbs, its wings, its neck. As if the forest itself felled this beast...

You hear a quiet, mad jabbering float across the clearing and track the noise to a figure in full plate armour, hugging its knees and rocking back and forth.

You could examine the dragon skeleton more closely ( 619 ) or approach the stranger ( 102 ). Of course, you could also simply travel to the North ( 330 ), or the South ( 546 ).

A customer says what they want, you give it to 'em. You get one wrong, you ruin my perfect reputation, and you're out. But hey, I'm sure you're a clever rabbit." He grins and points out your workstation, then steps away. "Let's get to it then."

In the next paragraph, there will be a list of the drinks you see in your station. You can find deeper descriptions of these drinks in the Items section of this book, but for every drink you examine you are keeping a customer waiting.

For each customer, roll a D20, divide the result by 4 and round down. That number is the tip they will be willing to give you, but that tip is reduced by 1 each time you refer to the drink’s list at the back of this book. If you choose the correct drink, you may keep whatever is remaining of the tip.

As soon as you step foot beyond the treeline, you sense movement behind you. You whip around to see what it was in a heartbeat, but there is nothing there.

Nothing but trees. The path to the exit is gone and all you can see now are those thick old-growth tree trunks blocking the way. Trying to look beyond those trees offers only darkness, and it's clear that you're trapped in these woods for now.

You turn back to the path and press on, coming to a junction quite quickly. The path splits out towards the East and the West, but you also notice a bright red cone-shaped object atop a tree stump ahead.

On looking closer, the cone suddenly shifts a little and you realise that it's sitting on the head of a creature that remarkably resembles the log left behind from a felled tree.

The creature shifts again, and you see some of the bark on its surface split and open to reveal a pair of eyes. It blinks sleepily at you but doesn't seem to be hostile.

30

Seeing the forest like this, already half destroyed, tells you one thing: the power in those old trees has been long fading. It can be put to better use. By you.

You remain where you float high above the trees and take in several deep breaths. With each lungful of air, the old growth beneath you withers and you become all the more empowered. The energy you accumulate feels God-like, and with it comes knowledge: this is far beyond the power that any of your Palapin ancestors ever used, and you now know where in the stars they retreated to. You can face them, demand answers for why they abandoned you, demand their return. Or end their cowardly kingdom, if they refuse.

One final breath and the forest beneath you is a graveyard of blackened tendrils curling in the light of day where once stood trees. No longer will a Mystic Wood grow on this world, but you now know that there are so many more worlds out there.

You look to the stars and continue floating upwards, your new mission of facing the creatures that created you clear in your mind.

This adventure is over, but a new one awaits you in the great beyond.

Congratulations, adventurer.

Considering its name and purpose, the slime organ is dry to the touch and remarkably firm. It feels like a water skein made of cartilage and, when squeezed, oozes a small amount of concentrated snail slime from its tip. A gross trophy most certainly, but you've heard such organs can have potent magical effects, with the right knowledge. Hoping to gain that knowledge, you add the Slime Organ to your inventory.

This is a druid's grave: a mage attuned to nature, capable of shifting into the shape of animals or of influencing the plants themselves. Now they have returned to nature, and surely they have no need of material items now?

Inside the box you find 2 Gold Pieces, a Potion of Plant Control, and a collection of nuts that still seem edible. Add 3 Food Items to your inventory.

All that's left to do is return down the path (turn to 79 ).

With the boat bobbing in place close to the shore, you carefully direct its prow across the river and place your magical conduit in the water behind. You feel the primal energies flow through you, and a trickle of bubbles starts to appear. It grows and grows in intensity, until that trickle of bubbles is an aggressive, chaotic, bubbling mass. But it has the intended effect: you start moving forwards, slowly then incredibly fast - catching air occasionally as the boat slices over small waves.

At the speed you reach, you estimate that you should have hit the other shore in less than a minute and yet it feels like an hour passes without striking land. You break your focus for just a moment to look ahead, and spy that you're only about halfway across the water. This river is indeed enchanted, but at least you have a way of speeding the journey along.

You check over your shoulder more often as you continue, slowing the boat down on approach to the shore so you don't crash painfully to a stop. Instead, you slide up the bank safely and the boat rests for a moment before the bow splits and falls clean open.

You are tired and the boat is spent, but your adventure can continue (turn to 468 ).

172

You pull the flute from your bag and play it like your life depends on it. Because it very well might...

In the wild, forest dragons are omnivorous but broadly prefer to eat plants. They graze often and have been seen swallowing hard objects like stones or gold to aid in the digestion of those vast quantities of foliage. But the more hungry a dragon is, the more desperate it is for meat. After a long period of dormancy, an adult forest dragon could easily hunt and devour a famer's full herd of cattle and still crave more. And your magic, unfortunately, has awakened that hunger in this young beast.

Before you even lower the flute from your lips, the creature lunges forward like a serpent and swallows you in two bites.

Your adventure ends here.

You realise the futility of fighting this maze-like magic. These woods are immeasurable powerful, and if their enchantment is breaking down then you cannot prevent it. It starts to rain. Not that it feels like it should, given the sun still shining and the eerie quietness of the rainfall. But why is it so eerie? What is wrong with the noise?

It hits you. You're expecting to hear rain striking leaves, that sharp whipping and slapping noise, but it's not there. In fact, as you look around, it seems that the rain is falling on you and you alone. It’s a cruel insult by the forest, but then the downpour stretches out before you, snaking through the woods and creating a muddy route forward. 208

The light you absorbed is benevolent, and so are you. You blink and, in an instant, you are transported to the ground at the head of a truly broken area of the wood. And in that desolated area, you see a machine-like beast beyond anything you recognise:

The first thing you see of the monster is an entire tree held sideways by a thin yet impossibly stiff clawed arm. The upper branches of the tree are shaking violently up and down, pine needles falling like snow as the trunk disappears sideways. You follow the motion and see that it is in fact being consumed bit by bit by the brutally bladed rotating maw of something entirely alien to you. The body of the monster is impressively bulky, with strange chitinous pipes bursting from the back of it and spewing the black smoke you've seen so often on your journey thus far. You can see why the spirit of the forest was scared: whatever this is devours the very woodland itself.

And, hanging above it on another strange arm, is an unconscious little boy in a cage. You would bet good money on it being the one you entered this forest to find.

Before it can see you, before it can even try to attack, you raise a hand. In that simple motion, the monster bursts into lights and disintegrates bit by bit - its glowing dust blowing into the wind. You have erased it not just from these woods, but from history. From the now, and the then, and the will be. With another wave of your hand, you transport the child into his own bed in the far village.

Then, you allow the power to run through you and into the ground. From the top of your head, from your fingertips, the energy recedes and leaves behind it a sense of calm. Not long after the last traces have left you, you see growth in this once dead land. Saplings of every kind sprouting from the wood chip strewn floor and shooting skywards, generations passing in an instant. Those fast-growing pines are suddenly blanketed by instant old growth, for the power you have gifted into the land has rejuvenated the forest to its core.

It was no small feat giving up that kind of power, and the forest will not forget it soon. You will have a home here as long as you live, which will be decades longer than expected thanks to the last remnants of that otherworldly magic inside you. Well done, adventurer.

"You have done an uncommonly kind thing for me," the monk says, genuinely touched. Perhaps that was the first great kindness he's been given since his exile? "I would like to provide a great kindness to you in turn."

"The hero that travelled to the Colosseum beyond the river, he entrusted me with a spare key to its doors. He knew that there is a fearsome beast at there and that he would have to face it, but should he fail someone else must succeed where he fell. There is a chance, albeit a slim one, that you could fight alongside him if he hasn't yet been defeated." The monk grips one of the huge beads of his necklace in both hands and twists. The two halves come away from each other and an iron key drops out, which he gives to you. "Please, use the key as soon as you approach the doors. Any delay whatsoever may risk you facing the beast alone."

"That is all I can offer you, my friend. And it is all I can drink," he laughs, patting his belly.

You follow the motion and see that it is in fact being consumed bit by bit by the brutally bladed rotating maw of something entirely alien to you. You know it to be searching for tokens that bear its likeness, but it’s the forest that suffers for the hunt. Then you see visions of a deer darting between trees, then it's a bear hauling a fallen log out of its way, then it’s a rat darting through the undergrowth. It faces the giant reptilian monster head on, not afraid for it has access to a greater power. You. It calls to you, it gives every whisp of its life so that you might be able to fight, and you do this brave little creature proud. The wild dragon is watching, waiting for you to make a move so that it can respond with deadly precision. Green dragons are intelligent fighters, they know the value of moving second.

You put two and two together and, given that this is a juvenile dragon and green dragon families are notoriously close, it's likely that this dragon is searching for its family. In time, and while ignoring roars and sounds of battle from within, you make enough of an opening beneath the wall to crawl under. You get on your belly and poke your head up into the arena, and what you see fills you with dread...

A beast unlike any you've seen before. Its head is enormous, like a merchant's cart on top of a thin neck but sporting a maw full of dagger-like teeth. The muscles at the joint of the jaw bulge and tense and you know from a glance that this creature is built for little other than combat. To balance this immense head, a long tapering tail extends out behind it and, in the middle, a massive muscular body joins the two. The creature stands on just two legs, powerful thighs and calves perched on three toes with claws at the end of each that could rend a person in half alone. But the most fearsome aspect of it are its arms: unusually long and spindly, and ending in a mass of jagged spines that you realise can move and snap together in a pincer like motion.

You are just in time to see those arms grip an adventurer in steel plate from many metres away and yank them towards the monster's mouth. In one quick bite, the battle is over and the hero falls to the ground, first one half, then the other.

You consider your next actions. Turn to 586 .

"What?" She goads. "I was hardly going to give you a weapon. Now come, great warrior," she says dryly. "Show me everything you have."

You need to think fast.

You don't see your own weapons anywhere, but there are supply crates nearby with various bits of steel and leather atop. There might be a weapon there for you to grab but she would surely strike you a blow as you do (1D20/4, rounded down).

Your hard work paid off, congratulations. You may either obtain a Dragon Bone Weapon, or a Dragon's Skull Helm.

You rest a moment, elated by your success and consider trying to release the other bone you spied, but the vines have other ideas. As if enraged that you bested them at all, you see those thick root-like tendrils squirm and twist, and tighten. The dragon's skeleton writhes in place, as if it were alive and fighting for its life once more. Then an almighty crack bursts out, sending wild birds soaring into the air. Every bone on that skeleton has been broken, something that you didn't think possible, but the forest clearly refuses to let you plunder its victim any further.

415

If this forest is going to be your end, you won't face it sitting still. If there has been anything you could rely on in your life, it's your own two legs and they surely won't fail you now. So you sprint on, even though you're certain you've seen the same tree over and over again. You ignore the identical patterns of flowers, you charge down the first path you see when junctions appear, you barrel your way forward and - at a point - simply start to enjoy the act of running. The freedom of it, ironic though it seems in this green labyrinth you find yourself in.

So lost in that runner’s high are you, that you don't even see the cliff's edge that you sprint off of.

You bounce down from branch to branch, for some time as far as you can tell. Eventually you manage to catch yourself, gripping the rough bark of a tree limb as if it were your final lifeline... When you look down, the ground is just a few feet away.

You sigh and let go of the tree.

The central area is a mess of tipped tables, broken chairs, detritus fallen from upper floors, and a thick layer of dust. In that dust, however, is a trail of freshly laid footprints walking from the bar towards the right of the building, disappearing beneath rubble.

You step forward and a great crash sounds out behind you! The ceiling has fallen where you were just standing. You are lucky to have your life, but the door to the inn is now completely blocked off. There's no turning around, you have to explore.

455

From what you can see, you have nothing to fear of this woman. If anything, she should be scared of you - a strange adventurer bursting into her home unannounced! So, you walk towards her with confidence, and pride, and you tell her that whatever was keeping her here has trapped her no longer.

She reaches out to grab your hand and her skin is soft against yours. But... Perhaps it's just a trick of this dim light, but you can't make out any detail on her face at all... This close up, you can make out the frills and fine stitch work of her dress, the way her shoes dig into her flesh just the slightest bit, but her face... Her face seems to be no more than vaguely shaped lumps where eyes, a nose, a mouth should be...

The grip on your arm becomes vice-like, the princess starts bending backwards at the waist and - you shudder to behold - she splits in two! Beady eyes blink out of her, fangs appear in the crevasse splitting her. You try to pull away but she's impossibly strong and those fangs lunge at you, sinking into your hip. You yowl out in pain (lose 4 Health), and kick the princess backwards.

Except it isn't a princess, but a mimic in the shape of one. And now you have no choice but to fight it.

456

How angry can these bees truly get? You only want a single globule of tar, after all, and a nest that size probably yields a ton of the stuff.

With that confidence in mind, you plunge your hand into the hive and grab a lump of Bee Tar. You pull it out and pop it in your pack and, for a moment, all seems well. And then it isn't.

The buzzing in the air that was a pleasant, if loud, white noise changes in pitch. It becomes feverish, and deafening, partly because - as you watch - a thick dark cloud of the insects forms and heads straight for you! You sprint away as fast as you can but, by the time the bugs lose interest, you're already victim to painful stings on every patch of exposed skin you have.

You're walking away with what you wanted, but was it worth it? Lose 5 Health.

457

You deftly clamber up the old elm tree and, with your arms held out for balance, you tight rope walk your way along the twisting branch towards the Colosseum wall. You have to leap the last few feet into the window, which you do with some grace, and find yourself in what must have once been the amphitheatre’s bathroom, judging from the drainage troughs leading to this window and the still lingering smell despite the generations it has lain disused. Lovely.

You walk further into the ancient building, finding your way to the great circular stands and gulping down the fresh air. From here, you have a clear view into the Colosseum arena, and what you see fills you with dread...

A beast unlike any you've seen before. Its head is enormous, like a merchant's cart on top of a thin neck but sporting a maw full of dagger-like teeth. The muscles at the joint of the jaw bulge and tense and you know from a glance that this creature is built for little other than combat. To balance this immense head, a long tapering tail extends out behind it and, in the middle, a massive muscular body joins the two. The creature stands on just two legs, powerful thighs and calves perched on three toes with claws at the end of each. But the most fearsome aspect of it are its arms: unusually long, and ending in a mass of jagged spines that move and snap together in a pincer like motion.

You are just in time to see those arms grip an adventurer in steel plate from many meters away and yank them towards the monster's mouth. In one quick bite, the battle is over and the hero falls to the ground, first one half, then the other.

You consider your next actions. Turn to 129 .

496

Just as the woman said, the ground beneath you starts to climb sharply as you travel North. The woods start to thin out, overtaken by only the most stubborn plants that can cling to the stone surface of this small mountain. It doesn't take you long to reach the peak, and from there you get a remarkable view of these woods.

Behind you, the forest is pure variety. A chaos at first glance, but there's logic to the old growth. Ancient trees and foliage winding and growing wherever nature saw best fit, and no single tree seems dominant. As such, there are more greens than you've ever seen in one place.

But to the North... the trees are regimented, grown in a strict grid pattern. There is also but one species: a quick growing softwood that bursts into maturity in a fraction of the time those ancient trees to the South do. This is no natural forest but one planned and cultivated. It is no wonder the mystic wood is dying...

To the East, you see clearings in the regimented growth structure, and what looks like trees that have melted at the tip like candle wax. Not far beyond that appears to be the source of the black smoke you've seen at various points on your adventure.

West of the mountain, the new growth forest stretches much farther and, at its most distant corner, you can see the distinct shape of an ancient Colosseum.

Just ahead of you, down the hill to the North, is what looks like a great crater. Perhaps the falling star you saw in the night?

The lake's water envelopes you, drags you down and robs you of any ability to float you may have once had. Like a pillow held against your head, you're pinned there with your hands on your neck, panicking and struggling.

You rise up your feet, amazed at being entirely unable to swim. Truly, it's not all that different from walking through the forest, except the light is dappled by the rippling lake's surface instead of the trees, and a rich assortment of fish fly around above you instead of birds. It's one of the most remarkable experiences of your life, but you must focus.

With tentative steps, you walk down to the water's edge and lower to your knees. You hold the chalice in both paws and place it on the ground, soon filling it with slime which congeals into a gross mass in the chalice's basin. You follow that up by uncorking the bottle of ale marked with a skull, immediately sending out a deathly stench of powerful booze. You cover your nose and pour the bottle into the chalice as well, which melts the slime into a thick-looking stew.

Finally, you grab the chalice once more and lower it into the lake until water rushes in over its rim. You pull it back up soon after, but that little amount seems to have been enough - the gloopy, foul liquid starts to glow and exude magical energy. You can only hope that magical energy does something to aid the inevitable taste of a brew such as this.

You followed Perceval's instructions. If he spoke true, drinking this will allow you to cross the lake. If he was lying, it will provide some truly unpleasant memories before the great beyond. Either way, there will be no turning back afterwards.

549

The ground underfoot becomes increasingly coated in flecks of splintered wood, and the new growth forest starts thinning out as you progress. Where once there were unnaturally grid-aligned trees, now there are unnaturally grid-aligned stumps.

You hear the source of this destruction before you see it. This horrible whirring, grinding noise which hurts your ears and vibrates your bones. And a splintering sound always comes with it, like a thousand woodsmen massacring a fallen tree at once. But it is something far worse than that…

The first thing you see of the monster is an entire tree held sideways by a thin yet impossibly stiff clawed arm. The upper branches of the tree are shaking violently up and down, pine needles falling like snow as the trunk disappears sideways. Sneaking forward, you can see that it is in fact being consumed bit by bit by the brutally bladed rotating maw of something entirely alien to you. The body of the monster is impressively bulky, with strange chitinous pipes bursting from the back of it and spewing the black smoke you've seen so often on your journey thus far. You can see why the spirit of the forest was scared: whatever this is devours the very woodland itself.

And, hanging above it on another strange arm, is an unconscious little boy in a cage. You would bet good money on it being the one you entered this forest to find.

You step out into the clearing before the beast, staring it down defiantly. You do not know if the thing has eyes but it certainly seems to regard your existence: it's bladed maw spins, it's pincer claws at the air, and fresh belches of awful smoke erupt from it. There are no tricks nor workarounds to be used. Just you, and an infernal beast that needs to be slain.

You focus as much heat into a patch of vines as possible, willing them to burn, and combust, and cinder. Knowing that dragon bones are remarkably resistant to heat, you hold nothing back and the results speak for themselves. Specks of glowing orange appear over the bark-like tendrils, then they start to glow from within brighter and brighter and brighter. For a flash, they're near painful to look upon but that burst of light is short-lived and all that remains are withered and charred remnants of the mighty growth that was there before.

You snatch a bone free. You may either obtain a Dragon Bone Weapon, or a Dragon's Skull Helm.

You rest a moment, elated by your success, and consider trying to release the other bone you spied. But the vines have other ideas. As if enraged that you bested them at all, you see those thick root-like tendrils squirm and twist, and tighten. The dragon's skeleton writhes in place, as if it were alive and fighting for its life once more. Then an almighty crack bursts out, sending wild birds soaring into the air. Every bone on that skeleton has been broken, something that you didn't think possible, but the forest clearly refuses to let you plunder its victim any further.

He notices you approaching and stands, a grin beaming across his bearded face. He is two heads taller than you and powerfully built, yet he embraces you in a gentle bear hug.

"Well met," he says and steps back, placing his hands on his hips. His voice is booming and has a slight accent to it. Perhaps he is from beyond one of the great seas. "My name is Roland," he says. "I am a knight, here to bring honour to my home and show that not all Northmen are raiders. And what is your journey, my friend?"

Your throat is hoarse after a while of it, but then you hear a shout calling back. You almost think it an illusion, a hallucination borne of hope, but the voice is unique and distinct to yours. It beckons you to follow it, and your keen sense of hearing allows you to track it down path after path. You're saved!

Eventually, you follow the noise through a wall of dense foliage.

"Take a seat, take a seat," the old halfling says without looking back. There is, however, nowhere to actually sit so you squat down just to rest your legs. It puts your head level with his.

The halfling turns holding the most delicate and perfect looking flute you've ever seen. Not a simple tube with holes, but a complex mastery of small levers and gears. The halfling pulls a few levers in practice and you see that with a simple finger movement multiple holes could be covered at once. But there was a lot of action that you couldn't see logic to as well: levers that move nowhere, gears that turn in a loop with no obvious result...

"What is this to you?" he asks, then puts his lip to the flute, pulls various levers, and blows. The note is familiar but also not. You would be certain that it was resoundingly unique, but the airiness of the man's breath doesn’t help.

You see this same sight dozens of times and you realise that this is how the forest cures itself. This is a battle for territory fought over centuries, not weeks in a bloody war.

There is only one path leading from the bridge, and something tells you that you're closer than ever before to your goals.

Turn to 11 .

595

You follow a thin trail from the hut, branches constantly reaching out and tapping you as you walk. The undergrowth grows thicker, a thin smattering of trees becomes a dense woodland, the ground beneath you changes from mud to a thick layer of intertwining roots - like a nest of snakes writhing and knotting in a dense mass.

Eventually you simply can't travel any further down this pass because the tree trunks are too close together. You're walking on pure roots at this point, and squeezing between the trees risks you getting stuck. You hear the gentle, rhythmic washing noises of a river just beyond this thick patch of forest, but you don't see it.

If you have keen sight, turn to 54 . Or, if you've heard a rumour about this patch of forest, turn to 15 .

Otherwise, you have no choice but to turn back (turn to 136 ).

596

You greedily suck air into your lungs, gulping it down and feeling the ache in your chest ease with every breath. Next, you become aware of a radiating soreness at the back of your head, likely where you were struck with something hard and heavy. Finally, you realise that your legs are chained to the largest lump of misshapen iron you've ever seen. You're trapped.

There is a woman standing over you, the cloth gag that had been shoved into your mouth in her hand. She has the steel helm of a knight in her other hand and is dressed in simple chainmail, a heavy amulet oozing magical power hanging from her neck. She has sharp features, with a pointed chin and angular cheekbones. Dark hair cascades down behind her, but does nothing to soften the icy glare she gives you.

"Wakey wakey, rabbit," she says. "I'm Marfisa. I came to this forest to get stronger, but old muscles over there hasn't made for much of a trainer."

She nods to the side and you follow her gaze to the cage. In it, the stranger you saw before lies still with the hilt of a crossbow bolt jutting out of his chest. You try to keep your breathing measured, in control.

If you have Prowess equal to or greater than 14, turn to 363 . Otherwise, turn to 406 .

597

She raises an eyebrow at you. "I'm Britomart, this is my shop. The name is very clever, obviously."

How do you respond?

“Your shop has no sign?”
What do you have for sale?”

Turn to 134
Turn to 497

Or continue your travels North ( 342 ), or East ( 316 ).

598

You shake your head and Weldo huffs, forcing the shell back into your hands.

If you'd like to try and convince him to just give you the flute, roll against your Charisma. If you're successful, turn to 443 . If not, turn to 503 .

Or you could attack the halfling and take the flute by force (turn to 482 ).

Or, of course, you could leave the hut altogether (turn to 103 ).

599

You try and argue that the princess he's seeking surely doesn't need saving at this point. She must have been in this forest for some time so she's either dead or quite happily settled.

Roland isn't overly pleased at your suggestion that his quest is pointless so, as politely as he can muster, he says that he respectfully disagrees and that he'd like to find her anyway.

If you have seen a princess in these woods, you could still tell him all about it (turn to 78 ).

Otherwise, you could attack Roland ( 501 ), or travel along the wide main road either North towards the bridge ( 39 ), or South ( 342 ). Or walk down one of the narrower cobblestone paths to the East ( 557 ), or the West 398 ).

600

Staring at it closer doesn't really offer you any new information. It is still a plain ring made of what looks to be gold. It is still on top of a note with "DO NOT TOUCH" written on it in black ink. It is still quite immobile.

Crouching beside the rock like this, you can see the woman's face though. She's young, perhaps early 20s, with wisps of dark hair falling free from a tied bonnet. Her eyes dart to you for but a moment, seemingly absorbing every detail of you in just that glance, then she turns back to the ring with a sneer. That action reveals a golden tooth which sparkles in the light.

If you have a way of detecting magic, you could try that now (turn to 350 ).

If not, you could suggest she try the ring on (turn to 283 ), or you could try it on yourself (turn to 139 ).

There is always the option to walk away to the East ( 20 ) or West ( 557 ), or even to attack the woman ( 218 ).

601

"D-dragon dragon," the stranger mutters, deep voice resonating in a tinny echo inside his helmet. "George. George George, Sir George, Saint George, George the Dragon Slayer," he mutters, still rocking back and forth.

You look between this broken man and the immense skeleton behind you, wrapped in vines.

"Did you kill this dragon?"
What's that amulet around your neck?"

Turn to 488
Turn to 61

602

The door swings open slowly, hampered by its weight, and reveals an open but scarcely decorated space. Light filters in from the far balcony doors, but much of the room is in gloom. You can make out a large four poster bed to one side, various cupboards and cabinets, as well as a vanity. It all seems oddly... neat.

Your attention is mostly fixed on the figure that darts into the middle of the room as you enter: the princess you saw from outside, in a billowing dress and with hair neatly tied up, but you can't make out any true details in the dark like this. Maybe if you were closer?

She extends a hand out to you...

If you have the means to detect magic, turn to 210 .

Otherwise, you could try talking to the princess (turn to 263 ). Or approach her and take her hand as she's gesturing for you to do (turn to 455 ). You could also stay your ground and see what happens (turn to 65 ).

603

A couple of hours pass of you serving customers with simple needs, namely ales, meads, and the occasional water (with at least a shot of something in). No one seems interested in the specialty items at all, until another curious customer approaches your station.

It's an amorphous green blob for the most part, crawling along the floor on a special mat that's laid out in front of it by the inn's servers. When it stops at your station, the blob quivers and jiggles, then a tendril emerges from it, plants itself on the bar top, and seems to strain as a larger column of slime rises. It's almost like the creature pulled a body out of that mass of goo.

The tendril on the bar starts to smoke and then it quickly withdraws, leaving a singed mark on the expensive wood. "Sorry," the slime says through a mouth splitting the jelly randomly near the top of the column. "I require acid. Your strongest," it says. Its voice is strained and strange; the nature of vocal cords made out of jelly, you suppose.

What bottle do you reach for?

A steel flask with glowing runes engraved into it

A sphere of reinforced metal, making a hissing noise

A curling Viking-like horn flagon
A glass bottle with 8 eyes and writhing spider legs
The decapitated head of a dark-haired man
A gelatinous looking bottle that wobbles on the shelf
A conical flask glowing with an intense white light
